URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS441799589	2016-11-11 01:52:23.0	11587.62	species	Red-breasted Parakeet	Psittacula alexandri			1				India	IN	Karnataka	IN-KA	Bangalore	IN-KA-BN					'J' Block, GKVK Campus	L5073172	P	13.086837	77.574773	2006-10-31	16:30:00	obsr359585	Subbu	Subramanya	S32468070	Stationary	EBIRD	15			1	0		0	0	0		Observing parakeet predation on maturing crop of maize	See, https://groups.yahoo.com/neo/groups/bngbirds/conversations/messages/10888--From: subbus@vsnl.com--To: bngbirds@yahoogroups.com--Subject: Red-breasted Parakeet in Bangalore--Date: Wed, 01 Nov 2006 02:09:23 +0000 (GMT)----Dear all,----Yesterday (October 31st) afternoon around 4.30pm I sighted what looked like a Red-breasted Parakeet (RBP) in a split-flock of over 100 Rose-ringed Parakeets (RRPs) at GKVK. This bird that looked a slight-slender version of RRPs had a distinct pink breast. ----The RRPs were there in force to raid a crop of maturing maize and were giving the labourers employed to scare them off – literally a run for their wages. As the labourers ran along sides of a vast field of maize shouting at the top of their voices, the parakeets seemed to play a game of &#96;catch-me-if-you-can’ as they took to wing at one end of the field - only to fly-over to the other side and settle on the crop. When couple of labourers joined forces and scared them from different sides of the field, the huge flock would split to sit on top of near-by trees, only to descend down surreptitiously to maraud the crop again. If unattended, in one or two sessions a single parakeet can completely strip a maize cob of its spathe and grains.----Initially, I was drawn to a strange sounding Kwank- Kwank- Kwank .. call that did not fit in with the screaming RRPs that sat on a nearby coconut palm, about 20 m away. The flock had just settled on the coconut canopy, and the birds were perched on every available frond. The parakeets sat on the fronds, each equally spaced from the other, as if they held between them an invisible tape-measure to say &#96;buddy keep your distance’. Against the bright sky, it looked as though each sloping frond had developed equally spaced green stubs. It took me a while, to single-out the strange caller and as it turned on its perch side-ways, the pink colour on its breast was clearly visible. The bird looked very much like a female RRP except for the pink breast - but strangely, it lacked grey head, broad black mustache and the golden patch on the wing – the other hallmarks of a true RBP.----There have been previous sightings of RBPs in Bangalore: the first being a fleeting glimpse of loner in a flock of RRPs by Shyamal in a wooded area inside the Indian Institute of Science on August 21, 1993 – a possible escapee from someone’s unattended cage. Subsequently on couple of occasions, a bird was seen flying with RRPs in the mornings in Sanjay Nagar by Ullhas Rane(?).----The present sighting only indicates that the RBP has prevailed in Bangalore over the years. The present bird could be the same individual (?), but the lack of grey head, broad black mustache and the golden patch on the wing indicate - that the bird to be altogether a new sub-adult – another possible escapee or the strange possibility of the species hybridizing with RRPs.----I am inclined to spend more time on evenings to try and see the bird again and also see if there are more of them - before the maize crop get harvested.----Cheers,----Subbu.	
URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS441799819	2016-11-11 02:01:18.0	11587.62	species	Red-breasted Parakeet	Psittacula alexandri			1				India	IN	Karnataka	IN-KA	Bangalore	IN-KA-BN					J Block GKVK	L4953706	P	13.086406	77.574924	2006-11-08	15:30:00	obsr359585	Subbu	Subramanya	S32468093	Stationary	EBIRD	10			1	0		0	0	0		Observing parakeets raiding a maturing crop of maize	1 raiding a maturing crop of maize along with a flock of 50+ rose-ringed parakeet--See, https://groups.yahoo.com/neo/groups/bngbirds/conversations/messages/10915----To: bngbirds@yahoogroups.com--Red-breasted Parakeet in Bangalore--Date: Wed, 08 Nov 2006 15:57:31 +0000 (GMT)--From: subbus@vsnl.com----Dear all,----Today afternoon, I sighted a Red-breasted Parakeet (RBP) again at GKVK. This time it was a male: with lilac-grey head, coral-read beak, broad black moustachial stripes descending from the base of its lower mandibles and turning sideways on the face. The mottled golden yellow patch on the wings were clearly visible, as much as the pink on its breast.----This bird was quite at home: totally consumed in a pastime of meticulously preening itself during mid-day amidst a flock 50-odd Rose-ringed Parakeets (RRPs) that appeared to have rented a dense canopy of a Jackfruit tree that grew close to the vast maize fields at GKVK. This sighting is the second one of the species over the last 9 days and sighting of this full-plumaged male could be an indication that there are at least two RBPs that visit GKVK area – the other being the one that was seen on October 31, 2006 (see my previous posting on this list - with the same subject).----This time again, it was the &#96;kwank-kwank-‘ call of the RBP that was so distinctly different from that of the usual screeching &#96;kreeick –kreeick’ of RRPs, that set me up to go and look for it. The &#96;kwank’ call was quite loud and audible enough from a distance of 40m.----These two GKVK sightings in addition to that of the one rescued by Sharath Babu at Girinagar and the past records of the species in Bangalore indicate that the RBPs are here to stay in Bangalore (please see related recent postings on this list). Unfortunately, we do not know the true status of the species in the city.----Cheers,----Subbu.
